  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_84b10654-98e4-4829-a2de-da1e83f375ab'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18440025808705237098">Dans leur téléphone, il y avait toute leur vie… New York. Aéroport Kennedy. Dans la salle d’embarquement bondée, un homme et une femme se télescopent. Dispute anodine, et chacun reprend sa route. Madeline et Jonathan ne s’étaient jamais rencontrés, ils n’auraient jamais dû se revoir. Mais en ramassant leurs affaires, ils ont échangé leurs téléphones portables. Lorsqu’ils s</span>
  <span id="freeText18440025808705237098" style="display:none">Dans leur téléphone, il y avait toute leur vie… New York. Aéroport Kennedy. Dans la salle d’embarquement bondée, un homme et une femme se télescopent. Dispute anodine, et chacun reprend sa route. Madeline et Jonathan ne s’étaient jamais rencontrés, ils n’auraient jamais dû se revoir. Mais en ramassant leurs affaires, ils ont échangé leurs téléphones portables. Lorsqu’ils s’aperçoivent de leur méprise, ils sont séparés par 10 000 kilomètres : elle est fleuriste à Paris, il tient un restaurant à San Francisco. Cédant à la curiosité, chacun explore le contenu du téléphone de l’autre. Une double indiscrétion et une révélation : leurs vies sont liées par un secret qu’ils pensaient enterré à jamais... Entre comédie romantique et thriller de haute volée. Une intrigue magistrale portée par des personnages bouleversants. Un final virtuose.<br /><br />Guillaume Musso donne toute sa saveur à cette comédie romantique mâtinée de thriller, dont le final témoigne de la rare virtuosité de l’auteur.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18440025808705237098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_1711708923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711708923" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711708923?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711708923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15382541693488158893">When I started reading this book from one of France's bestselling authors, I was expecting a somewhat clichéd love story about two people who accidentally exchange cell phones at the airport and find out about it when she's in Paris and he's in San Francisco. However, this novel took me on an adventure that I did not see coming, and I find that that's one of the charms of this story. It mixes chick-lit and romance with a whole other genre that I can't really tell on without spoiling it, and it d</span>
  <span id="freeText15382541693488158893" style="display:none">When I started reading this book from one of France's bestselling authors, I was expecting a somewhat clichéd love story about two people who accidentally exchange cell phones at the airport and find out about it when she's in Paris and he's in San Francisco. However, this novel took me on an adventure that I did not see coming, and I find that that's one of the charms of this story. It mixes chick-lit and romance with a whole other genre that I can't really tell on without spoiling it, and it does so really well. <br />The two characters were a tiny bit charicatured in the beginning, but I eventually learned to really like them and root for them. The same goes for the other characters and the different settings we get. In fact, I fell in love with the fact that this book mingles three worlds that I adore: the charm of Paris, the modern San Francisco and the rural England. <br />I was pleasantly surprised multiple times when reading this book that it only took me about a day to read, which says something about what a page-turner it is. If this is what Guillaume Musso's books are like, then it's definitely not going to be my last by him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15382541693488158893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5911504-dana-al-basha?shelf=translated-%D9%85%D8%AA%D8%B1%D8%AC%D9%85">translated-مترجم</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2530027901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer343601266564088642">I had the weirdest dream last night, I dreamt that I was reading this book in a cafe and liking it immensely and I started talking about it to some people. Maybe it should be my next read?<br/><br/>حلمت البارحة بأنني أقرأ هذا الكتاب في مقهى وقد أعجبني جداً وأبدأ بالحديث عنه مع الناس. ربما يجب أن يكون قرأتي القادمة؟<br/><br/>￼<img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566555707ra/28038482.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The translation sucks, it's filled with many errors. I don't think I can continue reading with this edition... or I might.<br/><br/>الترجمة سيئة جداً... مليئة بالاغلاط اللغوية والتعبيرية... لا أظن أنني أ</span>
  <span id="freeText343601266564088642" style="display:none">I had the weirdest dream last night, I dreamt that I was reading this book in a cafe and liking it immensely and I started talking about it to some people. Maybe it should be my next read?<br><br>حلمت البارحة بأنني أقرأ هذا الكتاب في مقهى وقد أعجبني جداً وأبدأ بالحديث عنه مع الناس. ربما يجب أن يكون قرأتي القادمة؟<br><br>￼<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566555707ra/28038482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The translation sucks, it's filled with many errors. I don't think I can continue reading with this edition... or I might.<br><br>الترجمة سيئة جداً... مليئة بالاغلاط اللغوية والتعبيرية... لا أظن أنني أستطيع قراءة هذا العمل بهذه الترجمة... أو ربما سأحاول<br><br>￼<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566555707ra/28038481.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yesterday, I begun reading Guillaume Musso's book The Call of An Angel, and I'm enjoying the read immensely, I even wanted to pull an all nighter but I felt extremely tired and fell asleep. The story revolves around Madeline, an owner of a flowers shop and Jonathan a bad tempered chef, who meet cross path in New York airport while going back to their home, her to Paris and him to San Francisco, only to discover that their phones have been switched and both of them start diving in the other's life and learn their secrets. Getting lost in a good book is the best feeling ever.<br><br>بدأت البارحة بقراءة كتاب غيوم ميسو "نداء الملاك" وكم انا مستمتعة بقرائته. كنت ارغب البارحة بقراءته في جلسة واحدة ولكنني أحسست بتعب حاد وغفوت. تتحدث أحداث القصة عن مادلين بائعة الورد وجوناثان الطاهي النزق اللذان يلتقيان أثناء سفر كل منهما إلى دياره في مطار نيويورك، حيث تعود هي إلى حياتها في باريس وهو يعود إلى حياته في سان فرانسيسكو، ليكتشفا أنهما بدلا هاتفهما ويبدأ الاثنان الغوص في حياة الآخر ومعرفة أسراره. كم هو جميل احساس فقد النفس في كتاب جيد...<br><br>￼<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566555707ra/28038480.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book shook my system! It began as a cute story with this traveling pinkish cover and turned into a suspenseful police book filled with mystery and murders not just one! I think that's why Musso is famous, he doesn't write romance, he writes crimes stories. This one is intense and very twisted.<br><br>هذا الكتاب ايقظ حواسي! بدا لي كأنه قصة ظريفة ذات غلاف زهري عن السفر ولكنه في الواقع كتاب مشوق وجنائي مليء بالاثارة وجرائم القتل وليس جريمة واحدة فحسب! أعتقد أن هذا سبب شهرة ميسو فهو ليس كاتب رومانسي بل كاتب جريمة. والقصة معقدة وحامية الوطيس.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566560993ra/28038806.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566560993ra/28038805.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566560993ra/28038804.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566560993ra/28038807.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1017523427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14408074616742107133">I'm almost tempted to give this book 5 stars for sheer entertainment value. Don't get me wrong, it was both terribly written and just batshit crazy, but I haven't laughed this much about a piece of writing in a long time. <br/>Having never read anything by Musso, I expected a standard, easy romcom - just what I was looking for after finishing the wonderful but extremely depressing Dead Zone. Little did I know that I would soon be thrown into a world of multiple feuding mafia families, several faked d</span>
  <span id="freeText14408074616742107133" style="display:none">I'm almost tempted to give this book 5 stars for sheer entertainment value. Don't get me wrong, it was both terribly written and just batshit crazy, but I haven't laughed this much about a piece of writing in a long time. <br />Having never read anything by Musso, I expected a standard, easy romcom - just what I was looking for after finishing the wonderful but extremely depressing Dead Zone. Little did I know that I would soon be thrown into a world of multiple feuding mafia families, several faked deaths and several attempted suicides and, my all time favorite: sharks that are used to dispose of dead bodies. <br />I would never recommend this book to anyone, but I can't say that I wasn't 100% entertained by it's unexpected insanity. </span>

  <i>"Il est des êtres dont c’est le destin de se<br/>croiser. Où qu’ils soient. Où qu’ils aillent.<br/>Un jour ils se rencontrent."<br/>-Claudie GALLAY</i>
</blockquote><br/>I really liked this one.The characters were really great,I loved their stories and the story itself was very captivating.I don't know why but I liked Jonathan more than Madeline,although I found Madeline's story much more fascinating.I liked the whole Alice thing,I liked the ending,but...even though I totally like Madeline and Jonathan together,I'm not sure I'm </span>

</blockquote><br>I really liked this one.The characters were really great,I loved their stories and the story itself was very captivating.I don't know why but I liked Jonathan more than Madeline,although I found Madeline's story much more fascinating.I liked the whole Alice thing,I liked the ending,but...even though I totally like Madeline and Jonathan together,I'm not sure I'm feeling the whole "insta-love" thing between them.Also...I <i>LOVE</i> all the quotes that Mr.Musso used at the beginning of every chapter!<br><br>Overall,quite enjoyable.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385348100ra/7130516.gif" width="300" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_490672822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/490672822" />
    <a title="Linh Bún" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15786257-linh-b-n"><img alt="Linh Bún" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424589073p2/15786257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/490672822?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linh Bún" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linh Bún" href="/user/show/15786257-linh-b-n">Linh Bún</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15786257-linh-b-n?shelf=never-get-enough">never-get-enough</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer490672822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11836296112969397745">I first came to Musso through "One day, perhaps", finished it and fell for him in the same day. Now after 5 hours dived in this new adventure, once again I found the very first feeling of "One day, perhaps" that seduced me, but in a different level. He has always been said to be the perfect combination of Marc Levy and Stephen King, I admit it's true. But now I think we seriously have to give him his own "brand" and start comparing other authors to him. <br/><br/>The story starts slowly and gotta say I fo</span>
  <span id="freeText11836296112969397745" style="display:none">I first came to Musso through "One day, perhaps", finished it and fell for him in the same day. Now after 5 hours dived in this new adventure, once again I found the very first feeling of "One day, perhaps" that seduced me, but in a different level. He has always been said to be the perfect combination of Marc Levy and Stephen King, I admit it's true. But now I think we seriously have to give him his own "brand" and start comparing other authors to him. <br /><br />The story starts slowly and gotta say I found it a lil' bit cheesy at first, you know, the plot and the characters are quite typical. But then it kept speeding up and pulled me from a secret to another till the last page of the book. Right when you found an answer, a dozens more appear. Just like Madeline on the case of Alice. All the details that seem so loose at first just fit in perfectly, and before you knew it, you were holding your breathe for so long, eager for the next detail to come and surprise you. It's the combination of romantic and detective novel, not the type of poorly arranged ones for cheaply sale, but the highest you can expect of it. How did he come up with all of that? From a coincidence of two strangers to murder, missing, kidnapping, cocaine trading, and love. The only thing I was not so sure about is the way two characters fell in love:)) maybe fall in love in 323 and have sex in 330 is a little bit fast for me :)) but it's destiny, you can't stop it rite :D<br /><br />I even found so much to think about from quotations he quoted at the beginning of each chapter. The way he took us from San Francisco to Paris, from England to the USA, from luxurious residences to slums... is like a magnificent trip with so much to learn. To sum up, definitely a "yes" to be on the all time favour list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11836296112969397745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16641296519744239983" style="display:none"><b>J'ai lu un livre en français!</b> <i>*Look at ME speaking French.*</i> Et je vais écrire mon review en anglais parce que c'est la vie ! <i>*Did that even make any sense?*</i><br /><br />Anyway, I finally finished <b>L'appel de l'ange</b> by Musso and it was....<i>weird.</i> And this review is going to be in English because I can't be funny while using French. <i>Let's all pretend <br /><br />Anyway, I finally finished <b>L'appel de l'ange</b> by Musso and it was....<i>weird.</i> And this review is going to be in English because I can't be funny while using French. <i>Let's all pretend that I'm actually funny. Thank you.</i><br /><br /><b><i>L'apple de l'ange is the story of two souls connecting together through an innocent chance. Or was it destiny?</i></b><br /><br /><u>Rating:</u> <b><i>3.5 stars.</i></b><br /><br /><u><b>Dumb Version of the Plot:</b></u><br /><br />So what had happend was: Jonathan and Madeline swapped phones. And since all of us are total creeps, they got to know each other by looking into each other's phones. Like any sane persone would do! Anyhow than things got complicated, like, OMG IS THIS REALLY HAPENNING? Kind of complicated. And you know, since this is Musso, ummm, They fell in luuurve. And there is action in there. Oh, and cooking because Jonathan is a cheif. And I really liked one character who is an assassin. I think that's it!<br /><br /><u><b>The Characters:</b></u><br /><br /><b>Jonathan:</b><br /><br />He was like the most bland soup I've ever tasted. I couldn't even try and pretend that he made me swoon. Maybe at the end but I think that's because I get emotional at night. He's a good dad, his wife left him and he was a famous chief blah blah blah and he's kind of cute. I couldn't really connect with him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I only related to him, that one time, when he tried to kill himself. She was a police woman. Girl Power! But she made stupid decision after stupid decision for her own desire. And wants me to think that she's the good guy! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She got a man killed to find this girl. And her only reaction was to not sleep at night! Say what? And then Jonathan tells her how his ex-wife killed a man. The dead guy was a douche. True. But Madeline's only response as a former policewoman: "Your ex-wife is smart. And he deserved it." I have a hunch that that's not what she was supposed to say. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Danny Doyle:</b><br /><br />He's the bad guy that made love him. And I don't care. Peace.<br /><br />As a conclusion, If you turn your brain off for a few hours and read this book: Fun! But if you actually think about some events. Your reaction will be similar to mine: WTF! And not in a good way. All in all I enjoyed it. I expected more from Musso and I was dissapointed And I came to the conclusion that his writing is good but his stories are kind of similar.<br /><br /><b><i>I hope you enjoyed reading this review and thanks!</i></b></i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423039221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17441309336076271889">Well, I read this book just because I'm in France and when I arrived it was the best-seller. I have to confess that I didn't are so much about the argument, I just bought it because of its position in the bookshelves, I wanted to know what were the Frenchmen reading. At first I was amazed that the book was a thriller, I mean, the people prefer the love stories for best-sellers, but I was making a mistake, it seemed like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/282080.Guillaume_Musso' title='Guillaume Musso' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guillaume Musso</a> was one of the best in the gender, and I really wanted to kn</span>
  <span id="freeText17441309336076271889" style="display:none">Well, I read this book just because I'm in France and when I arrived it was the best-seller. I have to confess that I didn't are so much about the argument, I just bought it because of its position in the bookshelves, I wanted to know what were the Frenchmen reading. At first I was amazed that the book was a thriller, I mean, the people prefer the love stories for best-sellers, but I was making a mistake, it seemed like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/282080.Guillaume_Musso" title="Guillaume Musso" rel="nofollow noopener">Guillaume Musso</a> was one of the best in the gender, and I really wanted to know why the people loved him so much. Well, I read the book. <br /><br />The first thing that I have to say is that I hate when the romantic story wins the race against the crude plot. In consequence, I have to say that French people love romance with a little bit of action, but essentially you have to give them romance, they will love you! Unfortunately, it doesn't work for me. I have already read another French authors like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/599793.Maxime_Chattam" title="Maxime Chattam" rel="nofollow noopener">Chattam</a>, and I think that he achieve managing the love story with the crude plot in a very consequent way, he leaves no open questions, there is no surrealistic situations, neither incoherent ones. Maybe I have not read enough books, but this one was not the Musso's masterpiece, I hope it isn't! ...I don't care either I don't want to read the other ones! Was it a bad book? No, it was not, maybe I had so much expectatives. I like the story, but I think that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/282080.Guillaume_Musso" title="Guillaume Musso" rel="nofollow noopener">Musso</a> could have done it so much better.<br /><br /><b>What I like</b><br />It was a funny story, you don't really know the role that the characters will play at the end of it. The main characters are very well constructed, I would have wanted the same for some of the others. I like the little world in the book, because yeah! everybody knows everybody of one way or another they are connected.<br /><br /><b>What I don't like</b><br />I have already say it, but I will repeat it, the love between the main characters hides the original story, I would have wanted a longer book, but with a story more detailed in the crime's details, I feel like I have a lot of questions that have been not answered. Moreover, sometimes it seems like the story is centred in Madeline and Jhonatan, and the rest of the world doesn't exist, I think it is not very professional to give all the weight to the protagonists, because it leave you without side stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17441309336076271889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6095652850090088876">As much as I've loved Musso's other books, I absolutely hated this one. This book was the most ridiculous book I've ever read. <br/>There's so much wrong with this book, I don't even know where to start. <br/>First of all the two main characters, Jonathan and Madeline are the world's two most deplorable people. They are incredibely rude, to each other, to basically everyone around them. The way Madeline treats amd speaks to Takomi, her Japanese helper at the flower shop, is disgusting. I felt like slappin</span>
  <span id="freeText6095652850090088876" style="display:none">As much as I've loved Musso's other books, I absolutely hated this one. This book was the most ridiculous book I've ever read. <br />There's so much wrong with this book, I don't even know where to start. <br />First of all the two main characters, Jonathan and Madeline are the world's two most deplorable people. They are incredibely rude, to each other, to basically everyone around them. The way Madeline treats amd speaks to Takomi, her Japanese helper at the flower shop, is disgusting. I felt like slapping her every time she opened her mouth. She is disrespectful and rude - maybe the writer meant to show her as a cool, self sufficiant, no-nonsense woman, but it so not come across that way. Jonathan is equally as rude. Marcus is laughably full of clishès, an archetypical dope-smoking American hobo who makes disgusting sandwiches, microwaves his underware in lieu of cleaning... Seriously?! Then Jonathan leaves his son in the 'capable hands' of Marcus for Christmas, because he falls in love with the woman he switched his phone with. OMG. Who does that??? Then they both start to snoop around in the stranger's phone (what? No password protection?). Again: Who does that? Then there are maffia links, mexican drog cartells, murders, a dead guy eaten by a shark, American witness protection... This book has it all. <br />Seriously, this book has felt like a teenager wrote it while high on something. Guillaume Musso was either high or seriously lost when he penned this crap. Sorry. But this should never have been published. It's a laughable attempt at crime mystery. Dear readers, give yourselves a break and give this a miss, unless you want to laugh your heads off while rolling your eyes. Ridiculous.</span>

I am so genuinely happy that I was sick just today, where the internet didn’t work and my friend left her b</span>
  <span id="freeText6216438073726895225" style="display:none">Initially I had no intention to read this book. I looked at it and thought ‘just another romantic novel’ just as all the others. I’m a classics girl. I love reading classics and YA novels just don’t get me. However, since my internet broke down and I was forced to stay in bed all day (having the flu....) I felt like I needed something to take my time. It’s now 4 hours and 400+ pages later. I am so genuinely happy that I was sick just today, where the internet didn’t work and my friend left her book at my place. It’s such an amazing and mind blowing plot line. Nothing in this plot was predictable- such a joy reading it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6216438073726895225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2179453813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2179453813" />
    <a title="Dridge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24518229-dridge"><img alt="Dridge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381674520p2/24518229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2179453813?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dridge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dridge" href="/user/show/24518229-dridge">Dridge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2179453813&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2179453813" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16792310433648645410">SPOILERS +++ SPOILERS +++<br/><br/>At its core, "L'appel de l'ange" has a really fast drive, which is probably the most important thing about a modern thriller. New revelations, new mysteries and new goals keep popping up throughout which keeps the reader flipping the pages. <br/><br/>I found especially the first half exciting: the two main characters Jonathan and Madeline go through each other's phones (exchanged by accident at the airport) and slowly discover little secrets about each other. Jonathan reveals via </span>
  <span id="freeText16792310433648645410" style="display:none">SPOILERS +++ SPOILERS +++<br /><br />At its core, "L'appel de l'ange" has a really fast drive, which is probably the most important thing about a modern thriller. New revelations, new mysteries and new goals keep popping up throughout which keeps the reader flipping the pages. <br /><br />I found especially the first half exciting: the two main characters Jonathan and Madeline go through each other's phones (exchanged by accident at the airport) and slowly discover little secrets about each other. Jonathan reveals via Madeline's online calendar that she is actively avoiding to get pregnant, he realises that her phone drive is partitioned (genius idea!)...<br /><br />But exactly this last revelation leads the book into the weaker half. Whereas the previous secrets and mysteries felt very believable, the second half relies too heavily on the reader's suspension of disbelief. Examples: Madeline used to work as a policewoman in Manchester (which this book makes out to be the most evil place on earth) where she worked on a kidnapping case of a young girl (Alice) and got involved with Manchester's "devil in person", the evil drug lord Danny. Jonathan's wife killed a man in self-defence and then faked photos showing her with another man because people wouldn't have believed her that she acted in self-defence. Madeline finds Alice's abductor due to him buying Oreo cookies in the same store she is in by accident,...<br /><br />I had in particular a problem with the Manchester part of the story: For once, I could not understand why Musso tried to make us want to like or at least be fascinated by Danny. He is a torturing, evil and terribly unwitty prick whom I and surely many other readers absolutely hated. Alice's unfortunate fate is at least remarkable, but again, Musso too desperately wants us to care. Which feels even more fraudulent once she has been freed from the claws of evil in the book's finale: Then, she is immediately discharged of the story and isn't even left a single word to speak, such as to say "Thank you" to her rescuers. Her sole existence in the plot is to cause a thrilling second half with a lot of chase scenes and to intertwine Jonathan's and Madeline's previous lives in a frankly contrived manner.<br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed reading this book (even more so as I did read the French original, an achievement I am childishly proud of) and would recommend it to thriller fans. But pump up your suspension of disbelieve, hard.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16792310433648645410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B0VD1MXcZeANffKzgDL+RSa1XltRTH9nyVxb1DxDKdtOMAgBV1lsSNBQSoKtT2APioanYKq+9fMiLkqVIzz0Ng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_55812634'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55812634-nio-liv?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Nio liv (Jana Berzelius #6)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7336461.Emelie_Schepp?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Emelie Schepp<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.52 avg rating &mdash; 99 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2020\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11201586227703413143\">Flerfaldigt prisbelönta deckarförfattaren Emelie Schepp är tillbaka med den sjätte delen om den fascinerande åklagaren Jana Berzelius i Norrköping.\n\nEn tidig aprilmorgon sprids en film på en ung man på Youtube. Han är misshandlad och har en spränglad<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11201586227703413143\" style=\"display:none\">Flerfaldigt prisbelönta deckarförfattaren Emelie Schepp är tillbaka med den sjätte delen om den fascinerande åklagaren Jana Berzelius i Norrköping.\n\nEn tidig aprilmorgon sprids en film på en ung man på Youtube. Han är misshandlad och har en sprängladdning fastsatt om kroppen. Polisen förstår att ett fruktansvärt öde väntar honom. De lyckas identifiera platsen men hinner inte fram förrän bomben exploderar. Det är den fjärde medlemmen i det kriminella nätverket Komados som har mördats på kort tid. Men rör det sig verkligen om samma gärningsperson? Kriminalinspektör Mia Bolander får hjälp av den nye utredaren Patrik Wiking att lösa fallen. Problemet är att ingen vill prata med dem. Ingen har hört något. Ingen har sett något. När Jana Berzelius dras in i utredningen inser hon att fallet har en direkt koppling till henne själv. Som åklagare har det alltid varit hennes uppgift att ta reda på sanningen. Nu får hon oväntad hjälp med att dölja den.\n\nNio liv är en högaktuell roman om våld och gängkriminalitet, och om de krafter som kan ta över när det finns något att skydda till varje pris.\n\nRöster om Emelie Schepps böcker:\n\n&quot;En av de bästa deckarna jag läst någonsin.&quot; Anna Jansson, författare till serien om Maria Wern\n\n&quot;Jana Berzelius är en fascinerande och originell karaktär som saknar motstycke i kriminallitteraturen.&quot; Nerikes Allehanda\n\n&quot;Så välgjort och drivet berättat att Schepps stora läsarskara kommer att sluka Broder Jakob med nöje.&quot; Borås Tidning\n\n&quot;Och lycklig den som inte upptäckt Emelie Schepp förut ...&quot; Göteborgs-Posten\n\nEmelie Schepp har tidigare släppt fem böcker i serien om åklagare Jana Berzelius. Böckerna har tillsammans sålt i två miljoner exemplar, nominerats till Stora ljudbokspriset, utsetts till Årets deckare,samt blivit bästsäljare i flera länder. Emelie Schepp har utsetts till årets deckarförfattare (Crimetime Specsavers Award) 2016, 2017 och 2018. Hon bor i Motala tillsammans med sin familj.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11201586227703413143\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2506332427426510862">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. H</span>
  <span id="freeText2506332427426510862" style="display:none">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. He came home to France with his head filled with ideas for novels. The readers can easily see the influence his time in the United States has had on him, as the action in his books takes place overseas. He currently teaches in a high school in the south of France, all the while working on his novels. His first published novel was with Editions Anne Carriere in 2001: <i>Skidamarink</i>, this novel did not reach out to the masses however, but his following novels published on XO Editions have all been hugely successful, some of them translated into 20 languages. His novel, <i>Afterwards</i>, has been adapted to the big screen and was in cinemas January 2009, starring John Malkovich, Evangeline Lily and Romain Duris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2506332427426510862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
